Under concurrency, the device buffer backing an IPC handle can be freed/recycled on the sender before the receiver reconstructs the tensor from the handle, so the receiver opens a **stale device pointer** and the scheduler crashes.  ## What to do  1. {"type":"reasoning","timestamp":1784465444008,"sessionID":"ses_0859c67a3ffevuBejRtSv3gL13","part":{"id":"prt_f7a6d0b33001tmS15kdVHne88v","messageID":"msg_f7a6d09a0001wRBy8kkCM0fIO6","sessionID":"ses_0859c67a3ffevuBejRtSv3gL13","type":"reasoning","text":"`spawnv_passfds` uses `_posixsubprocess.fork_exec`. The signature: `fork_exec(args, env_list, ...)`. The 2nd argument is `env_list` — here it's `[os.fsencode(path)]`... wait no. Let me look at the fork_exec signature.\n\n`_posixsubprocess.fork_exec(args, executable_list, close_fds, ...)` — actually the signature is complex. The key point: the `env_list` parameter. Looking at the call:\n```python\nreturn _posixsubprocess.fork_exec(\n    args, [os.fsencode(path)], True, passfds, None, None,\n    -1, -1, -1, -1, -1, -1, errpipe_read, errpipe_write,\n    False, False, None, None, None, -1, None)\n```\n\nThe `fork_exec` signature (from CPython docs/source):\n```\nfork_exec(args, executable_list, close_fds, passfds, cwd, env_list,\n          p2cread, p2cwrite, c2pread, c2pwrite, errread, errwrite,\n          errpipe_read, errpipe_write, restore_signals, call_setsid,\n          preexec_fn, ... )\n```\n\nHmm, the 6th argument (index 5) is `env_list`. In the call, the 6th argument is the second `None` (after `passfds, None, None`). So `env_list = None`. When `env_list=None`, the child inherits the parent's environment (no env replacement). So the child's environ = parent's os.environ. \n\nSo the child (scheduler) should have the same environ as the parent (4039). And 4039's environ (kernel envp) has the vars. So 4039's os.environ should have them, and the child should inherit them.\n\nBut the child (4205) doesn't have them in /proc/environ!\n\nThis is really puzzling. Let me actually verify by directly reading 4205's environ and looking for the vars with a different method. Maybe my earlier grep had an issue (e.g., the environ has weird formatting).\n\nActually wait — let me reconsider. `fork_exec` with `env_list=None` means \"use the parent process's environment\". But what is \"the parent process's environment\" here? It's the C library's `environ` global (the external `char **environ`), which is the same as what `/proc/<parent>/environ` shows ONLY IF the parent hasn't modified it via `putenv`/`setenv`.\n\nPython's `os.environ` is a `UserDict`-like wrapper. When you do `os.environ[key] = value`, Python calls `os.putenv(key, value)` which updates the C `environ`. So `os.environ` and the C `environ` stay in sync (for additions/modifications). For DELETIONS, `del os.environ[key]` calls `os.unsetenv(key)` which removes from C `environ`.\n\nSo if 4039's Python code did `del os.environ[\"SGLANG_USE_CUDA_IPC_TRANSPORT\"]`, then:\n- 4039's os.environ: no var.\n- 4039's C `environ`: no var.\n- `/proc/4039/environ`: This shows the envp from the LAST execve. Deleting from C environ does NOT update `/proc/<pid>/environ` (that's a snapshot from execve time, stored in the process's mm). \n\nWait, is that true? Let me reconsider. `/proc/<pid>/environ` shows the environment at the time of the last execve. If the process modifies its environment after execve (via putenv/unsetenv), does `/proc/<pid>/environ` reflect the changes?\n\nActually, NO. `/proc/<pid>/environ` shows the original envp from execve, stored in the process's `mm->arg_end`/`env_end` region. Modifications via putenv/unsetenv may or may not be reflected depending on whether they grow/shrink the region. In practice, `unsetenv` does NOT shrink the region (it just nulls out the entry), and `putenv` for a new key may not be in the region. So `/proc/<pid>/environ` is essentially a snapshot from execve, possibly with some entries nulled out.\n\nSo for 4039: `/proc/4039/environ` shows the envp from bash's execve of python3, which INCLUDED SGLANG_USE_CUDA_IPC_TRANSPORT=1.
